рдореВрд▓рдореН - рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд░рдореН

рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрдГ

рдЕрде рд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрд╕рд░рд░реВрдкрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддреЗрд░реНрдореГрддреНрдпреНрд╡рдиреНрддрдХрд░реВрдкрддреНрд╡рдВ рддрджреНрд░реВрдкреЛрдкрд╛рд╕рдирд╕реНрдп рдлрд▓рдореН, рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдЪрдпрдирд╕реНрдпрд╛рдореГрддрддреНрд╡рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдВ рдлрд▓рдореН, рдкрд░рд┐рд╢реНрд░рд┐рджреНрдпрдЬреБрд╖реНрдорддреАрд▓реЛрдХрдВрдкреГрдгреЗрд╖реНрдЯрдХрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛ рддреГрддреАрдпрдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгреЗ рдкреНрд░рджрд░реНрд╢реНрдпрддреЗ- рдПрд╖ рд╡реИ рдореГрддреНрдпреБрд░рд┐рддрд┐ ред ‘рдореГрддреНрдпреБрдГ’ рдЖрдпреБрд╖рдГ рдХреНрд╖рдкрдпрд┐рддрд╛ ред рд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрд╕рд░рд╕реНрдп рдореГрддреНрдпреБрд░реВрдкрддреНрд╡рдВ рд╡реНрдпрдирдХреНрддрд┐- рдПрд╖ рд╣рд┐ рдорд░реНрддреНрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдорд╣реЛрд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдорд┐рддрд┐ ред рдкрд░рд┐рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдореН ‘рдЕрд╣реЛрд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдорд╛рдпреБрдГ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгреЛрддрд┐’ рд╣рд┐рдирд╕реНрддрд┐, “рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгреБ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд╛рдпрд╛рдореН”- (рдзрд╛. рдкрд╛. рдд. рдк. рек) рдЗрддреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд░реВрдкрдореН ред ‘рдЕрде’ рдЖрдпреБрдГрдХреНрд╖рдпрд╛рдирдиреНрддрд░рдВ рдореНрд░рд┐рдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред рд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрд╕рд░рдореГрддреНрдпреБрд░реВрдкреЛрдкрд╛рд╕рдХрд╕реНрдп рдлрд▓рдорд╛рд╣- рд╕ рдпреЛ рд╣реИрддрдВ рдореГрддреНрдпреБрдорд┐рддрд┐ ред рдПрд╡рдВ рд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрд╕рд░реЛ рдореГрддреНрдпреБрд░рд┐рддрд┐ ‘рдпрдГ’ рдЙрдкрд╛рд╕реНрддреЗ рдЕрд╕реНрдп ‘рдЖрдпреБрдГ’ рдЖрдпреБрд╖реНрдпрдВ ‘рдЬрд░рд╕рдГ рдкреБрд░рд╛’ ‘рдПрд╖’ рд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрд╕рд░реЛ ‘рди’ рд╣рд┐рдирд╕реНрддрд┐ рдорджреАрдпрдВ рд░реВрдкрдорд╕реМ рдЬрд╛рдирд╛рддреАрддреНрдпрдиреБрдЧреНрд░рд╣рдмреБрджреНрдзреНрдпреЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдорд╛рдпреБрд░реЗрддрд┐ рее рез рее

Eggeling
  1. The Year, doubtless, is the same as Death; for he 1 it is who, by means of day and night, destroys the life of mortal beings, and then they die: therefore the Year is the same as Death; and whosoever knows this Year (to be) Death, his life that (year) does not destroy, by day and night, before old age, and he attains his full (extent of) life.

Eggeling
  1. And he, indeed, is the Ender, for it is he who, by day and night, reaches the end of the life of mortals, and then they die: therefore he is the Ender, and whosoever knows this Year, Death, the Ender, the end of his life that (Year) does not reach, by day and night, before old age, and he attains his full (extent of) life.

Eggeling
  1. They went on praising and toiling, striving to win immortality. Praj─Бpati then spake unto them, ‘Ye do not lay down (put on me) all my forms; but ye either make (me) too large or leave (me) defective: therefore ye do not become immortal.’

Eggeling
  1. He spake, ‘Lay ye down three hundred and sixty enclosing-stones, three hundred and sixty Yajushmat─л (bricks), and thirty-six thereunto; and of Lokampr╠ес╣З─Б (bricks) lay ye down ten thousand and eight hundred; and ye will be laying down all my forms, and will become immortal.’ And the gods laid down accordingly, and thereafter became immortal.

Eggeling
  1. Death spake unto the gods, ‘Surely, on this wise all men will become immortal, and what share will then be mine?’ They spake, ‘Henceforward no one shall be immortal with the body: only when thou shalt have taken that (body) as thy share, he who is to become immortal either through knowledge, or through holy work, shall become immortal after separating from the body.’ Now when they said, ’either through knowledge or through holy work,’ it is this fire-altar that is the knowledge, and this fire-altar that is the holy work.

Eggeling
  1. And they who so know this, or they who do this holy work, come to life again when they have died, and, coming to life, they come to immortal life. But they who do not know this, or do not do this

holy work, come to life again when they die, and they become the food of him (Death) time after time.

  1. But when he builds the fire-altar, he thereby gains Agni, Praj─Бpati, the Year, Death, the Ender, whom the gods gained; it is him he lays downy even as the gods thus laid him down.

рдЪрдпрдиреЗрди “рд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрд╕рд░рдВ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рдордЧреНрдирд┐рдорд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐” рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдордирдиреНрддрд░рд╛рддреАрддрдЧреНрд░рдиреНрдереЗ (рд╢. рдк. резреж ред рек ред рей ред резрез) рдЙрджрд┐рддрдореН, рддрджреЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╢рджрдпрддрд┐- рдкрд░рд┐рд╢реНрд░рд┐рджреНрднрд┐рд░реЗрд╡рд╛рд╕реНрдп рд░рд╛рддреНрд░реАрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддреАрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ ред рдкрд░рд┐рд╢реНрд░рд┐рддрд╛рдВ рд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд┐рд░реВрдкрддреНрд╡рдВ рдпрдЬреБрд╖реНрдорддреАрдирд╛рдорд╣реЛрд░реВрдкрддреНрд╡рдВ рдЪ (рд╢. рдк. резреж ред рек ред реи ред реирен) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЧреБрдХреНрддрдореН ред рдпрдЬреБрд╖реНрдорддреАрднрд┐рд░реЗрд╡рд╛рд░реНрджреНрдзрдорд╛рд╕рдорд╛рд╕рд░реНрддреБрдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐рд░реБрддреНрддрд░рддреНрд░ рд╡рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрддреЗ- “рддрддреЛ рдпрд╛рд╢реНрдЪрддреБрд░реНрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддрд┐рд░рд░реНрджреНрдзрдорд╛рд╕рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рд╕реНрддрд╛ рдЕрд░реНрджреНрдзрдорд╛рд╕рд╛рдирд╛рдореЗрд╡ рд╕рд╛ рд╜рд╜рдкреНрддрд┐рдГ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрддреЗ рд╜рд░реНрдзрдорд╛рд╕рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдорд╛ рд╜рде рдпрд╛ рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢рдорд╛рд╕рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рд╕реНрддрд╛рдорд╛рд╕рд╛рдирд╛рдореЗрд╡ рд╕рд╛ рд╜рд╜рдкреНрддрд┐рдГ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрддреЗ рдорд╛рд╕рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдорд╛ рддрд╛ рдЙ рджреНрд╡реЗ рджреНрд╡реЗ рд╕рд╣ рд╜рд░реНрддреБрд▓реЛрдХрд╛ рдЛрддреВрдирд╛рдорд╢реВрдиреНрдпрддрд╛рдпреИ”- (рд╢. рдк. резреж ред рек ред рей ред резреп) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд▓реЛрдХрдВрдкреГрдгрд╛рднрд┐рд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдХрд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрдореБрд╣реВрд░реНрддреНрддрд╛рдирд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ ред рддрд╛рд╕рд╛рдВ рдореБрд╣реВрд░реНрддреНрддрд░реВрдкрддреНрд╡рдореБрдХреНрддрдореН рее резреи рее

  1. By the enclosing-stones he gains his nights; by the Yajushmat─л (bricks) his days, half-moons, months, and seasons; and by the Lokampr╠ес╣З─Бs the muh┼лrtas (hours).

Eggeling
  1. Thus the enclosing-stones, supplying the place of nights, are made the (means of) gaining the nights, they are the counterpart of the nights: there are three hundred and sixty of them, for there are three hundred and sixty nights in the year. Of these, he lays twenty-one round the G─Бrhapatya, seventy-eight round the Dhishс╣Зya hearths, and two hundred and sixty-one round the ─Аhavan─лya.

Eggeling
  1. Then the fifth (layer):–five asapatn─Бs, forty vir─Бjs, twenty-nine stomabh─Бg─Бs, five n─Бkasads, five pa├▒cac┼лс╕Н─Бs, thirty-one chandasy─Бs, eight (of) the G─Бrhapatya hearth, eight (of) the Puna┼Ыciti, two seasonal ones, a vi┼Ыvajyotis, a vikarс╣З─л, a naturally-perforated one, the variegated stone, the fire which is placed on the altar–these one hundred and thirty-eight are (in) the fifth layer.

Eggeling
  1. All these make three hundred and ninety-five. Of these, three hundred and sixty, supplying the place of days, are made the (means of) gaining the days, they are the counterpart of the days: There are three hundred and sixty of them, for there are three hundred and sixty days in the year. And for the thirty-six (additional days) which there are 10 the filling of earth (counts as) the thirty-sixth; and twenty-four thereof, supplying the place of half-moons, are made the (means of) gaining the half-moons, they are the counterpart of the half-moons. And the (remaining) twelve, supplying the place of months, are made the (means of) gaining the months, they are the counterpart of the months. And, lest the seasons should be wanting, these (twelve bricks), by two and two (taken) together, supply the place of seasons.

Eggeling
  1. And as to the Lokampr╠ес╣З─Б (space-filling bricks), supplying the place of muh┼лrtas (hours), they are made the (means) of gaining the muh┼лrtas, they are the counterpart of the muh┼лrtas: there are ten thousand and eight hundred of them, for so many muh┼лrtas there are in the year. Of these, he lays down twenty-one in the G─Бrhapatya (altar), seventy-eight in the Dhishс╣Зya-hearths, and the others in the ─Аhavan─лya. So many, indeed, are the (different) forms of the year: it is these that are here secured for him (Praj─Бpati, the Year), and are put on him.

Eggeling
  1. Now, some wish to get this total amount 11 in the ─Аhavan─лya itself, arguing, ‘Those are different brick-built fire-altars: why should we here (in the ─Аhavan─лya altar) take into account those laid down there (in the G─Бrhapatya and Dhishс╣Зyas)?’ But let him not do so. There are, indeed, ten of these fire-altars he builds–eight Dhishс╣Зyas, the ─Аhavan─лya and the G─Бrhapatya–whence they say, ‘Agni is Vir─Бj (wide shining or ruling),’ for the Vir─Бj (metre) consists of ten syllables: but, surely, all these (altars and hearths) are looked upon as only one, as Agni; for it is merely forms of him that they all are,–even as the days and nights, the half-moons, the months, and the seasons (are forms) of the year, so are they all forms of him (Agni).

‘рдЕрдирддрд┐рд░рд┐рдХреНрддрд╛рдГ’ ‘рдЙрдкрд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдГ’ рдЕрддрд┐рд░реЗрдХрд╛рднрд╛рд╡реЗрдиреЛрдкрд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдГ рдХрдердВ рднрд╡рдиреНрддреАрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╢реНрдирд╛рд░реНрдердГ ред рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реАрд╕рд╛рдпрдгрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╡рд┐рд░рдЪрд┐рддреЗ рдорд╛рдзрд╡реАрдпреЗ рд╡реЗрджрд╛рд░реНрдердкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЗ рдорд╛рдзреНрдпрдиреНрджрд┐рдиреАрдпрд╢рддрдкрдердмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрднрд╛рд╖реНрдпреЗ рджрд╢рдордХрд╛рдгреНрдбреЗ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереЗ рд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЗ рддреГрддреАрдпрдВ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдореН рее (резреж-рек-рей) рее

Eggeling
  1. As to this they say, ‘How are these (bricks) of his laid down so as not to be excessive?’ Well, these (bricks) are his (Agni’s) vital power, and man’s vital power is not excessive. Thus whosoever, knowing this, performs this holy work, or he who but knows this, makes up this Praj─Бpati whole and complete.
